  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3ac86785-f90b-473a-b528-4c2bb5e1f447'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer8858397151914476274"><i>Peer-e-Kamil</i> (English: The Perfect Mentor) is a story focusing on a deviational sect which violates the finality of our Prophet (P.B.U.H) meanwhile, narrating a heart wrenching journey of two unhappy souls; Salaar Sikandar, a genius with an outstanding I.Q who has complicated queries about life and Imama Hashim, an ordinary girl with a stable family. Both are poles apart i</span>
  <span id="freeText8858397151914476274" style="display:none"><i>Peer-e-Kamil</i> (English: The Perfect Mentor) is a story focusing on a deviational sect which violates the finality of our Prophet (P.B.U.H) meanwhile, narrating a heart wrenching journey of two unhappy souls; Salaar Sikandar, a genius with an outstanding I.Q who has complicated queries about life and Imama Hashim, an ordinary girl with a stable family. Both are poles apart in terms of spiritual awakening. Destiny maneuvers their lives to cross each other’s paths, until Salaar falls in love with Imama after facing a horrifying experience that totally changes the course of his life.<br />It was published in Shuaa Digest from July 2003 to February 2004.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780124826" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14438010069393169145"><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b> What is next to esctacy?<br/>Pain.<br/>What is next to pain?<br/>Nothingness.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>OMG !<br/>Peer-e-Kamil is my most favourite and the first Umaira Ahmed's book that I read, following her other books.<br/>Salar was an obnoxious guy that I hated most. He gradually transformed into a good guy and the story of his transformation and "realization of self" is what Peer-e-Kamil is about.<br/><br/>Many people criticize about Salar's I.Q. level and that why he is shown as an extra-ordinary guy. Please guys, when it comes to "the model of </span>
  <span id="freeText14438010069393169145" style="display:none"><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b> What is next to esctacy?<br />Pain.<br />What is next to pain?<br />Nothingness.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />OMG !<br />Peer-e-Kamil is my most favourite and the first Umaira Ahmed's book that I read, following her other books.<br />Salar was an obnoxious guy that I hated most. He gradually transformed into a good guy and the story of his transformation and "realization of self" is what Peer-e-Kamil is about.<br /><br />Many people criticize about Salar's I.Q. level and that why he is shown as an extra-ordinary guy. Please guys, when it comes to "the model of inspiration" as a modest man, we always exemplify the best.<br /><br />This is the book that changed my outlook on life. The book that made me realized where I stand in other's lives. That its never about how pretty you are, how rich you are or how genius you are. The moment you disappear into shadows, people forget about you. <br /><br />The only thing matters is how good you are as a person, as a human being. How compassionate you are towards those others. How you can inspire and postively change lives of others. How you can show them the right path. How you can be the light guiding them when they are blinded by the negativity and arrogance.<br /><br />I would recommend every urdu reader to read this book. </span>

<div id="review_188237358" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188237358" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5862550-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557438942p2/5862550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188237358?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/5862550-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5862550-sana?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188237358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11764723742486611231">Peer-e-Kamil was my second Urdu novel and first by Umaira Ahmed. Being one of the most popular Urdu novels to be ever written, Peer-e-Kamil is a journey from a bad extreme to a good extreme. And it is justified. Yes, it gets somewhat unbelievable to ponder over the changes in Salaar, the protagonist, but we know all the reasons. That's the beauty of it all.<br/><br/>Set against the backdrops of Islamabad, America, Paris and Lahore; Peer-e-Kamil tells the story of a boy blinded by his own misgivings about </span>
  <span id="freeText11764723742486611231" style="display:none">Peer-e-Kamil was my second Urdu novel and first by Umaira Ahmed. Being one of the most popular Urdu novels to be ever written, Peer-e-Kamil is a journey from a bad extreme to a good extreme. And it is justified. Yes, it gets somewhat unbelievable to ponder over the changes in Salaar, the protagonist, but we know all the reasons. That's the beauty of it all.<br /><br />Set against the backdrops of Islamabad, America, Paris and Lahore; Peer-e-Kamil tells the story of a boy blinded by his own misgivings about life. It is his journey into a man who is a complete opposite of the boy he was.<br /><br />At first, the subtly persuasive personality of Umaima irritates and amuses Salaar. But as the time goes on, he cannot understand his obsession with her. All he did was spend a few hours with Umaima, but those few hours and the words that were exchanged between them, haunts him. They come into his mind when he least expects them to, making him question his way of living life. Ultimately, his thoughts force Salaar headfirst into depression and he finds nothing worth living for. He tries to pray, but fails miserably.<br /><br />Being an extraordinary student, he has always been so far gone heady into the feeling of superiority that he is ever unable to decipher the meaning of 'Siratum Mustaqeem' or the right path. He doesn't know what the right path constitues and why it is for humans led astray. And of all the people he has ever met in life, he loathes the one who claims to be religious. Those people are the worst because to him they just exaggerate everything about themselves to the hilt.<br /><br />Time goes on and Salaar finds himself changing. His transformation is complete during the late hours of the night when he is tied to a tree wearing only his Bermuda shorts. There he truly understands the next levels of ecstasy, the thing that always eluded him. This scene reminded me of a somewhat similar scene from Brida by Paulo Coelho.<br /><br />Peer-e-Kamil is about following the path of righteousness. It is about un-deterring faith in the face of every difficulty in life. It teaches a profound lesson about how to live and how our life will achieve a meaningful stage. It is about finding ourselves through our Creator. Peer-e-Kamil is about the search for life itself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11764723742486611231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026282095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17491507927916542461">I bought this book with very high expectations, but I was bitterly disappointed. The story is entirely based on themes of dissatisfaction regarding ones life and religious belief. Now, such a sensitive topic has extensively been discussed in literature, but this writer dealt it with most amateur manner. She adamantly resorted to humiliate a religious minority (whose beliefs are much contradictory to the Islamic teachings) and used most derogatory language against the spiritual leader of this par</span>
  <span id="freeText17491507927916542461" style="display:none">I bought this book with very high expectations, but I was bitterly disappointed. The story is entirely based on themes of dissatisfaction regarding ones life and religious belief. Now, such a sensitive topic has extensively been discussed in literature, but this writer dealt it with most amateur manner. She adamantly resorted to humiliate a religious minority (whose beliefs are much contradictory to the Islamic teachings) and used most derogatory language against the spiritual leader of this particular religious group. This is highly undesirable. <br /><br />Other than that the story held no allure for me at all. The case for the protagonist’s redemption was not contested by the author with good rationale or logic. The story too was very weak and rather predictable. Pick up any Urdu novel and you will find a spoiled, eccentric millionaire protagonist who is strayed and lost. Here, the girl jumps in, a little struggle and she makes a good man out him. Lo and behold, a perfect recipe for a bestseller in Pakistan. (Oh how I hate it )<br /><br />A huge disappointment.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17491507927916542461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Imama had certain dreams for which she was working really hard, however her life changes completely when she starts </span>
  <span id="freeText985528069224077973" style="display:none">As far as I can remember, this might be the first time I have read a full novel in Urdu and I must say it was really impressive. Before this I have read quite a few short stories but nothing more than that.<br /><br />The story revolves around two characters, Sallar and Imama. Two extremely different personalities who come together in the end not by sheer coincidence but due to their destiny. Imama had certain dreams for which she was working really hard, however her life changes completely when she starts to take interest in the religion of Islam. <br /><br />It is said that in life we don’t get what we really want, we get what we need and that is what happens with Imama. On the other hand, Sallar achieves everything from academics to career to his marriage. For him, Imama and her true believe in Islam is the source of it all, therefore according to him she is much more in control of her life than him. <br /><br />Though at times, the story is a bit too stretchy, hence I gave it four stars. Despite that, it was a powerful, captivating and an interesting narrative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="985528069224077973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I don’t think I’ve ever read a story as powerful and beautiful as this one. <br/><br/>This book and story is very rich, very powerful and is definitely a very beautiful story that truly touched my heart and soul on so many levels, how and why, that I can't put in words.   <span id="freeText2287389807109047545" style="display:none">I seriously have no words to describe <b> HOW MUCH I LOVED </b> this book and story. I don’t think I’ve ever read a story as powerful and beautiful as this one. <br /><br />This book and story is very rich, very powerful and is definitely a very beautiful story that truly touched my heart and soul on so many levels, how and why, that I can't put in words. It made me think of so many things and honestly there were times when it shook me from inside. It's filled with emotions, morals, lessons, bitter realities (that we all fail to understand or even if we do we deny it) and what not. While I was reading it I just couldn't put it down and the moment I finished, I got lost in thoughts for hours. I usually don’t read a book again once I’m done reading it no matter how much I loved it but this is that one book I’m willing to make an exception for as I want to read this book again and again. This book and the story is <b> AMAZINGLY AMAZING.</b> Everyone should read it once but with a clear mind and should try to understand the depth of the story.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_92933875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92933875" />
    <a title="Anum " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2485455-anum"><img alt="Anum " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570866293p2/2485455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92933875?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anum " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anum " href="/user/show/2485455-anum">Anum </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485455-anum?shelf=urdu">urdu</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485455-anum?shelf=5-stars-amazing">5-stars-amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2485455-anum?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92933875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10884762727459866724">I adored this book! Umaira Ahmad has succeeded in writing a book that holds much more substance than the average love story. Indeed, I don't believe that this story can be put in the romance category at all. <br/><br/>It seems to deal with life in general, rather than anything else. With such amazing charisma, Umaira Ahmad has written this profound novel on how a man with so many talents is surpassed by an average girl, when it comes to arriving on the path of righteousness.<br/><br/>It is a book about how man is n</span>
  <span id="freeText10884762727459866724" style="display:none">I adored this book! Umaira Ahmad has succeeded in writing a book that holds much more substance than the average love story. Indeed, I don't believe that this story can be put in the romance category at all. <br /><br />It seems to deal with life in general, rather than anything else. With such amazing charisma, Umaira Ahmad has written this profound novel on how a man with so many talents is surpassed by an average girl, when it comes to arriving on the path of righteousness.<br /><br />It is a book about how man is nothing and no one to anyone else but himself, and that it is entirely up to him if he wants to save himself. In addition, Salar exemplifies that a person has no one to be afraid of but his/her Lord, the Almighty and the only one who can possibly damage you is Him. However, where He loves you and gives you so many chances to redeem yourself, you are your own worst enemy. You have only yourself to fight off and save your life.<br /><br />Immama, on the other hand, is the epitome of sacrifice. A girl who has given up her everything, in order to do what she feels is the right thing. Being a woman in a society that is not kind to that part of the female population, which chooses to think for themselves, she portrays how, when you believe in God's power and His mercy, you will never be disappointed. <br /><br />Even more so, this novel seems to be about, how everything happens for the best. The characters are embedded in a world, where everything goes wrong just to turn out right for them. It reminds me so very much of 'surah Yousaf' in that regard.<br /><br />However, Jalal Ansar, remains a rather enigmatic character to me. He seems too good in the first half of the novel. So much so that, I was rather annoyed with his perfection. He seemed to be a good man, who was just caught up in circumstances, which were not in his power to handle. However, in the second half, he turns out to be a right jerk. His transformation to the Omniscient reader seems to be a little too rushed. I think Umaira Ahmad should have worked out his personality a little more thoroughly. <br /><br />Overall, I believe that this book was a very well-written piece by the author. <br /><br /><br />EDIT: <br /><br />As I have grown older, I have realised that some of the themes in the book are not dealt very well. A woman's religious conversion story is one thing. However, the uncalled for attack on a religious group in Pakistan was very problematic and irresponsible on part of the author. I wish she would have handled the subject objectively rather than let her own bias towards a people blind her into spewing hate, intolerance and sectarianism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10884762727459866724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785898993" />
    <a title="Fahad Nasir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35426300-fahad-nasir"><img alt="Fahad Nasir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515841794p2/35426300.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35426300-fahad-nasir?shelf=devastating">devastating</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35426300-fahad-nasir?shelf=juliets-mine">juliets-mine</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785898993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10071100287499632122"><b>"What is next to ecstasy?"</b><br/><br/>Wandering around with unfocused eyes, unhinged mind, I feel distant; too distant from this world that I knew just yesterday. Snapping back to reality used to be relatively easier, it's not anymore. I... Have never cried this hard for a book, for any character, and yet I wish I could... cry harder. <br/><br/><b>"... pain."</b><br/><br/>Despite the ache in my eyes and the crushing pressure inside my skull, I read and kept reading this book from 2 to 8 last night/morning. Several times I slapped wat</span>
  <span id="freeText10071100287499632122" style="display:none"><b>"What is next to ecstasy?"</b><br /><br />Wandering around with unfocused eyes, unhinged mind, I feel distant; too distant from this world that I knew just yesterday. Snapping back to reality used to be relatively easier, it's not anymore. I... Have never cried this hard for a book, for any character, and yet I wish I could... cry harder. <br /><br /><b>"... pain."</b><br /><br />Despite the ache in my eyes and the crushing pressure inside my skull, I read and kept reading this book from 2 to 8 last night/morning. Several times I slapped water on my face to keep myself going. From one to page to another I flipped... <br /><br /><b>"What is next to pain?"</b><br /><br />... till I could take it no more and yet I felt myself go on. I wonder what magic had Miss Umera Ahmed laced within these words, that this story, this journey, kept me gripped like none other. <br /><br /><b>"... nothingness."</b><br /><br />... And nothingness do I feel right now. I have only the second time in my life felt <i>this</i> way... And a part of me wishes I stay engrossed within this forever. It's a delectable system.<br /><br /><b>"What is next to nothingness?"</b><br /><br />Where do I go from here, I wonder? It's not like no book has made me change the way I looked at the world before, but this... oh, this just doesn't feel like a book; it's something more. Pir-e-Kamil (SAW) absorbed me in such a manner that I... became Salar, Imama. I distantly felt what they felt, went through what they did and the torture seemed so sweet that I can't describe. Like a little baby, I hugged this book at one point and cried with sobs evolving within my chest. I still wish I could cry harder. <br /><br /><b>"... hell."</b><br /><br />These book writers, they amaze me. They possess the tendency to fiddle with us readers' emotions in the most reckless of manner and yet we fall in love with them. You'd marvel how one could come up with a plot so perfect and otherworldly. [Whilst reading] It now feels as if I had peeled strips of my skin off and adhered them to this book. Next came bones and finally my flesh. Only once I had completed reading did I felt the full blow that figurative separation of my own body brought to me.<br /><br />But I do know one thing though, that I do not part away from this book. This story dug deep within me - maybe much more than it did for others - and it augmented the size of my soul after crawling those depths. The pieces have gone in, they are now settling soothingly. I can sense it. I can feel them working themselves in a beautiful way... </span>
  <a data-text-id="10071100287499632122" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7539319951647358771">peere kamil is about the AHMADI group. it's religious based novel described the story of two persons having different beliefs and thoughts. Peer-e-Kamil is an extraordinary novel written by Umera Ahmed. It revolves around two main characters, Imamah and Salaar.<br/> totally fell in love with this novel! A lot of my friends recommended it to me and I read it in less than 3 days. It’ s such a great story and it’s a page-turner for sure. It shows the people who love Allah and their Messenger and how peo</span>
  <span id="freeText7539319951647358771" style="display:none">peere kamil is about the AHMADI group. it's religious based novel described the story of two persons having different beliefs and thoughts. Peer-e-Kamil is an extraordinary novel written by Umera Ahmed. It revolves around two main characters, Imamah and Salaar.<br /> totally fell in love with this novel! A lot of my friends recommended it to me and I read it in less than 3 days. It’ s such a great story and it’s a page-turner for sure. It shows the people who love Allah and their Messenger and how people change by the will of Allah through other people. It’s spiritual and very relatable. I’m sure there are people who go through such phases in life, in fact I think everyone gets a chance at least once in their lives. It also depends on who want that change. Surely, Allah listens and knows what’s in our hearts.<br /><br />Anyway, I’d like to say again that Peer-e-Kamil S.A.W.W is an amazing read! It’s definitely worth reading and I recommend it to everyone! If you like reading, you can’t miss this novel! And even if you’re not a fan of reading, you have to read it! ;) :D<br />I’m sure you will fall in love with it, everyone I know who’s read it did! :) I may not be able to express in words how amazing it is, that you’ll have to find out yourself ;) I promise you won’t be disappointed!<br /><br />Umera Ahmed has done a wonderful job with this novel! This has got to be her best novel. I think that’s why she doesn’t want to make it into a drama; because reading this novel has it’s own magic and she probably doesn’t want that magic to disappear. I myself wouldn’t want it to go away. Hats off to Umera Ahmed for writing such a masterpiece! I really want her to write more novels with that magic in them!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9481928406862996289">Let me get this straight first,I like Umera Ahmed and i think everyone in Pakistan does.Well, because dramas based on her book adaptations are awesome and give people like me a cause to fangirl <i>(especially if they cast fawad khan).</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448956269i/17213613.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So she is a pretty common household name even my grandfather who is seventy-ish knows about her.<br/>so you can say, her immense popularity compelled me to expect A LOT from Peer e Kamil. It's not like I hate the book or something. I have a "it's not you, its me" kind of re</span>
  <span id="freeText9481928406862996289" style="display:none">Let me get this straight first,I like Umera Ahmed and i think everyone in Pakistan does.Well, because dramas based on her book adaptations are awesome and give people like me a cause to fangirl <i>(especially if they cast fawad khan).</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448956269i/17213613.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So she is a pretty common household name even my grandfather who is seventy-ish knows about her.<br>so you can say, her immense popularity compelled me to expect A LOT from Peer e Kamil. It's not like I hate the book or something. I have a "it's not you, its me" kind of relationship with it. This was my first book by Umera Ahmed and before that I read Jannat Ke Pattay and Mushaf. I loved JKP BUT tolerated Mushaf. YOU know why? because both had the same format. They are great books if read after giving Urdu lit some space but the problem is reiteration of the same concepts . It was written in 2004 AND its has not been made into a drama so it leaves a lot of ground for other people to copy her. Infact a lot of screenplays resemble Peer e Kamil.<br><br><br>I wont discuss Salar's way to piety or Immamah's conversion to Islam because they overshadow a lot of good and bad concepts discussed in the book. <br><br><b>Social stigma faced by AH who must not be named:</b><br>YEAH, i am actually saying it. I don't support them or anything but how would you feel when you walk in a room and everybody starts whispering.I am not talking about adults well because they are adults but kids?They believe in the tooth fairy too.<br><br><b>Pakistani Compassion:</b><br> Characters like Saeeda ama actually exist in reality and there are people like her who take in orphans. She was really adorable and her main-tankhaw-se-le-ke-jute-ka-size-puchun-ge wali nature was something not very original but very close to reality.<br><br><br><b>The big question:</b><br>"Why does a women brings a man towards sirat e mustakeem".Haven't they heard of the thing called DIY.<i>Magar is mein kya hairani wali baat hai pakistani mard to pani bhe khud uth ke nae pe sakte.</i>It's a very exploited concept and jannat ke pattay was a breath of fresh air since jahan causes haya to rethink her lifestyle and not vice versa.<br><br><b>Statistical probability of love/hate at first sight.:<b><br>I just don't get it.<br><br><br><br><br><br></b></b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5835015676476240567">It's a very profound novel; it will hook you up till the end. The more you read the more it urges you to read. <br/>The story revolves around Imama Hashim and Salar Sikander. Imama is a religious girl, seeking a right path towards Islam.   <span id="freeText5835015676476240567" style="display:none">It's a very profound novel; it will hook you up till the end. The more you read the more it urges you to read. <br />The story revolves around Imama Hashim and Salar Sikander. Imama is a religious girl, seeking a right path towards Islam. Where Salar is totally opposite of her, he even doesn't perform salah (namaz)... having an IQ level of 150+ makes his parents proud but he takes life non-seriously.<br />Imama run away from her house. She was compelled to do this act because of her family sect. On the other hand Salar is in need to know the answers of his questions. <br />"What comes after ECSTASY?" 'PAIN' she said "What comes after pain?" 'NOTHINGNESS' "What comes after nothingness?" 'HELL' "and what comes after that?" ''Aren't you afraid to know what comes after hell, where you have left your everything behind" Imama's answer was going above his head but in nine years he experienced all by himself that she was right in every way.<br />"To what extent I will love you, I do not know. This is the matter of the heart and I have no control over my heart. But this I do know that as long as we are together, I will be faithful and obedient to you. This within my purview. I will be with you at every difficult point of our lives; no matter what life throws at us, I will be there with you as your support. I have become a part of your life in good times; if things change and we face adversity I will be by your side"<br />It consists of very wise sayings which will touch your heart for sure, no doubt it's an exceptionally well written novel. It will en gross you till the last the page.<br />Where they met? What made them fall in love each other? What has come in their life to change their personality? Did Imama find the right path in the end? How they suffered in their life? After running away, did she finds a safe spot? To get the answers of all questions above, you need to give a read on this novel.<br />This beautiful novel have not been turned into a drama because of showing differences of sect (shia sunni issues) <br />Later this novel has translated in English also and It is preceded by "Aab-e-hayat"</span>

<div id="review_2957847991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2957847991" />
    <a title="Omama." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50052704-omama"><img alt="Omama." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605117659p2/50052704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2957847991?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Omama." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Omama." href="/user/show/50052704-omama">Omama.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/17205102-peer-e-kamil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50052704-omama?shelf=%D8%A7%D8%B1%D8%AF%D9%88-%D8%A7%D8%AF%D8%A8">اردو-ادب</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2957847991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10754553262150647380">I read this book in my early teens, when the mind was naive, and the spirits were high. It was the type of book which I’d read in one setting, and would want to re-read again immediately after finishing. I really can’t recall how many times I’d had read this book. Obsessing over Salaar’s character, his gradual transformation from a hedonistic and over-indulgent boy to a sober and noble humanitarian, Imama’s painful and alone journey after she left her family to protect her ‘Iman’ to the outer wo</span>
  <span id="freeText10754553262150647380" style="display:none">I read this book in my early teens, when the mind was naive, and the spirits were high. It was the type of book which I’d read in one setting, and would want to re-read again immediately after finishing. I really can’t recall how many times I’d had read this book. Obsessing over Salaar’s character, his gradual transformation from a hedonistic and over-indulgent boy to a sober and noble humanitarian, Imama’s painful and alone journey after she left her family to protect her ‘Iman’ to the outer world, was all so euphoric. Some of the parts in the book bring you a lot of motivational and religious vibes. Some of the lines were totally awe-inspiring for me. <br /><br /><b> What is next to ecstasy? <br />Pain.<br />What is next to Pain? <br />Nothingness. <br />What is next to nothingness? <br />Hell. The place which has nothing ahead, everything’s left behind. </b> <br /><br />Argh!!! You would get a shudder, goosebumps by just reading and understanding these lines. The ‘pure’ romance conundrum which finally unites the protagonists in the end, is the only reason people are so in awe of this book. <br />But as I grew up, as the mind developed and got used to seeing the inevitable injustices, prejudices, hatred and religious indifferences around the society, I felt this story targets a certain population on the base of religion, which points towards intolerance and bigotry. But I dont think Umera Ahmed should get all the hatred for writing this, as we are born with this hypocrisy and intolerance. It’s in our blood. Furthermore, I have found Umera Ahmed’s writings to be extremely predictable and coincidental; you would always know what’s going to happen next. Overall, the novel does highlight the societal moral, social and religious aspects ; sketching a typical male dominated society, and how things can go tough for a girl If she takes a step on her own. <br />Lastly: this is the most overrated novel of the decade, and I’m glad I grew up. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10754553262150647380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1908702304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1908702304" />
    <a title="Peter Upton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57424462-peter-upton"><img alt="Peter Upton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507186775p2/57424462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1908702304?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peter Upton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter Upton" href="/user/show/57424462-peter-upton">Peter Upton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789690023414" href="/book/show/13643734-pir-e-kamil">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57424462-peter-upton?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1908702304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15624618299173920098">Initially, I was disappointed with this book and I didn't know whether it was the translation into English that was the problem. It felt disjointed to me as though each sentence was a statement in its own right rather than being a flowing conversation, almost as though the book was in a rush to get somewhere more important and was painting all of the background scenes in a hurry but gradually as the book progressed either the translation skills improved or the story line gripped me so much that </span>
  <span id="freeText15624618299173920098" style="display:none">Initially, I was disappointed with this book and I didn't know whether it was the translation into English that was the problem. It felt disjointed to me as though each sentence was a statement in its own right rather than being a flowing conversation, almost as though the book was in a rush to get somewhere more important and was painting all of the background scenes in a hurry but gradually as the book progressed either the translation skills improved or the story line gripped me so much that I didn't notice anymore and I ended up thinking this was the best novel I had read in the last 30 years since James Clavell's 'Shogun'.<br />The story line is based around Imama a young girl of the Ahmadi community and an offshoot sect of the Muslim religion who secretly converts to the traditional Muslim faith and rather than go through with the arranged marriage to another member of her community and sect, which she had previously been happy to agree to, she now decides to run away from home even though this means giving up the medical studies she is devoted to and leaving the family she loves. And as a Father from the West with totally different values and spiritual views I found myself getting angry and scared for her that someone with so much intelligence could be so lacking in commonsense and not realize how dangerous the world can be for a girl in a big city without family or friends and how in loving her family she was loving God.<br />To escape she enlists the help of her next door neighbour Salar and I couldn't escape the feeling that everything else in this book had been written to accommodate the story of Salar. To be born into a rich family can be a curse, to be born with an IQ of 150+ can be a double curse and Salar is doubly cursed. With nothing materially to strive for he immerses himself in drugs, pornography and prostitutes. With all knowledge immediately known he strives only for that one piece of knowledge that defies him; what is it like to die? In search of this one piece of knowledge, he makes repeated suicide attempts probably in the hope of being resuscitated with this knowledge intact. It is easy to condemn him but I remember many years ago reading in the newspaper of a young genius who did commit suicide leaving behind a note with just one word of explanation on it 'Bored'. I should also mention that Salar is without any morals or any conscience whatsoever.<br />It is to this person that Imama runs in her escape attempt and he agrees to drive her into the city not out of any desire to help a girl in distress but out of having something unusual happening to spark his interest. He clearly sees all the mistakes she is making but watches with amusement as she makes them, like a person who opens the door of the budgerigars' cage to let it escape while knowing that the wild birds will try to kill it. By now the book had entrapped me and I was fascinated by the philosophical argument going on during the car journey into the city as Salar, who admits he is a bad person, points out to Imama, a good person, the paradox of their situation that he is doing good by helping her while she is doing bad by running away and breaking her parents hearts and exposing them to humiliation in the eyes of their community. If she was truly good wouldn't she have put the good of her family above her new found religious faith? <br />Salar drops Imama off to disappear into the city centre and drives away without compunction, regret or any knowledge of where she intends to seek sanctuary but a tiny mustard seed of Imama's devout nature has entered unseen into his soul. We then follow Salar over weeks and months and years as he follows his education path and the occasional, amused moment of wondering what had become Imama gradually turns into concern and worry and then despair as the previously unknown concepts of guilt and grief and yes even morality grow within him. As an adult seeking redemption he devotes his life to good works and charitable actions but the guilt will never let him go until he reaches the bottom, the dark night of the soul that takes him onto the religious path.<br />'In life, at sometime or another we come to a point where all relationships cease, where there is only us and Allah (God). There are no parents, brothers or sisters, or any friend. Then we realize that there is no earth under us nor is there any sky above, but only Allah who is supporting us in this emptiness.' (I have been there and this is true.)<br /> But still the guilt will not let him go but to tell you more would spoil the story. There are so many highs and lows still to be endured, so many twists and turns that I have not mentioned here and some of the writing is just exquisite. Definitely a five star book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15624618299173920098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_896925338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/896925338" />
    <a title="Bushra Joyo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14033821-bushra-joyo"><img alt="Bushra Joyo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351447780p2/14033821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/896925338?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bushra Joyo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bushra Joyo" href="/user/show/14033821-bushra-joyo">Bushra Joyo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer896925338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9432244938987838860">Warning: Spoiler Alert <br/><br/><br/>Pir e Kamil was not my everyday Judith McgNaught fairy tale story where a beautiful girl who belongs from an underprivileged background falls in love with a ruthless handsome prince and in the end everything gets lovely. Well yes in this story as well everything gets better in the end but the non linear structure Umera Ahmed has given to the story is simply beautiful.<br/><br/>The damsel does not leave her comfortable life for the love of a man but she leaves all her comforts only f</span>
  <span id="freeText9432244938987838860" style="display:none">Warning: Spoiler Alert <br /><br /><br />Pir e Kamil was not my everyday Judith McgNaught fairy tale story where a beautiful girl who belongs from an underprivileged background falls in love with a ruthless handsome prince and in the end everything gets lovely. Well yes in this story as well everything gets better in the end but the non linear structure Umera Ahmed has given to the story is simply beautiful.<br /><br />The damsel does not leave her comfortable life for the love of a man but she leaves all her comforts only for what she believes in. Her faith is unwavering and her determination is inspiring. Her love for Jamal is as human as it can be. She does not fall in love for the handsome, rich and spoilt brat but she falls in love with a person she thought is an ideal.<br /><br />Our knight is not enjoying the riches he has been bestowed upon since childhood. He is disturbed and finds solace only after he understands the gravity of his foul actions. He is sourly punished before he gets his reward.<br /><br />What I so loved about this novel was the utmost faith the characters had. The story told us that devil was an angel in the beginning and not every saint has a crystal clear past. We all have our stories and we all have our faults. We are individuals and what our families do and are associated with us might reflect on us but that doesn't mean those choices made by our families are our own as well. The key is to forgive and move on. The right thing to do is not to judge on past actions but on current situations. There is no black and white but different shades of grey in which we all are.<br /><br />A must read for all the literature fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9432244938987838860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AvmHQejy9ge3YZzbddLkjIjo/cd5Ap+UfZd9uqMbbRNMkvtGMcYcNZ8E5RgLIHkFMm8yXQN0xuM1WFSzt+wtwA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0FKB1DljGIPW9F1NsPPrAG7NIjeu4+0PX2udbSKaD1SeOf3T4Ffysf6RJI7OAXaJ1ErtrdSVtHgXpLRkNm1Phw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_9632002'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9632002-raja-gidh?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Raja Gidh / راجه گدھ<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/962207.Bano_Qudsia?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Bano Qudsia<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.18 avg rating &mdash; 2,551 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1981\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer2747072121707243557\">Raja Gidh (Urdu: راجه گدھ) by Bano Qudsia is one of the most widely read and acclaimed Urdu novels. Gidh is the Urdu word for a vulture and Raja is a Hindi synonym for king. The name anticipates the kingdom of vultures. In fact, parallel to the main <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2747072121707243557\" style=\"display:none\">Raja Gidh (Urdu: راجه گدھ) by Bano Qudsia is one of the most widely read and acclaimed Urdu novels. Gidh is the Urdu word for a vulture and Raja is a Hindi synonym for king. The name anticipates the kingdom of vultures. In fact, parallel to the main plot of the novel, an allegorical story of such a kingdom is narrated. The metaphor of the vulture as an animal feeding mostly on the carcasses of dead animals is employed to portray the trespassing of ethical limits imposed by the society or by the religion.\n\nBano Qudsia has written this novel drawing on the religious concept of Haraam and Halaal. Many readers tend to interpret Raja Gidh as a sermon, in which Bano Qudsia puts forth her theory of hereditary transmission of Haraam genes. Naturally the plot is woven to support the thesis. In the opinion of many readers and critics she manages to convince them that the pursuance of Haraam, be it financial, moral or emotional, results in the deterioration of a person\'s normality in some sense. She seems to suggest that the abnormality is transferred genetically to the next generation.\n\nApart from the above implication the novel has many social, emotional and psychological aspects. The nostalgic narration of the historical Government College Lahore and of the Lawrence Garden Lahore lights upon the days of seventies and eighties.\n\nBano Qudsia is among those Urdu writers who would think ten times before writing a sentence. But she does not sacrifice the flow of the narrative anywhere in this novel. Her characters are not black and white ones as some of the critics would like to suggest. Every sensitive reader who has attended a college or a university in a Pakistani setting is bound to find some similarities between themselves and one of the characters.\n\nPlot: Seemin Shah, hailing from an upper middle class family, falls in love with her handsome class fellow Aftab in the MA Sociology class at Government College Lahore. Seemin is a modern and attractive urban girl and attracts most of her male class fellows, including the narrator (abdul)Qayyum and the young liberal professor Suhail. Aftab belongs to a Kashmiri business family. Though he also loves her, he can not rise above his family values and succumbs to his parent\'s pressure to marry someone against his wishes and leave for London to look after his family business. Now the long story of separation begins.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2747072121707243557\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div type=\"hidden\" name=\"book_id\" id=\"book_id\" value=\"9632002\" />\n<input type=\"hidden\" name=\"name\" id=\"name\" value=\"to-read\" />\n<input type=\"hidden\" name=\"unique_id\" id=\"unique_id\" دیا۔\n کتاب میں گیارہ مضامین ہیں جو بہ ظاہر ”ہولا خبطا پن“ کے شاہکار ہیں مگر فی الحقیقت سوسائٹی اور تمدن کی دکھتی رگوں کو چھوا ہے اور خامکاریوں اور سفیہانہ رواسم وتوہمات کا پردہ فاش کیا ہے۔ پطرس نے اپنا مطلب زیادہ تر مزاح میں طنز کی پُٹ دے کر نکالا ہے۔ بخلاف دیگر ظرافت نگاروں کے جو تمسخر کو آلہٴ کار بناتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ ان کے مضامین میں باوجود اس احساس کے کہ ہم کو (اور معاف کیجئے گا آپ کو) بےدال کا بودم بنایا جا رہا ہے جھنجھلاہٹ کے بجائے گدگدانے کی ادا نکلتی ہے اور اسی کے ساتھ غو وتعمق کی دعوت ہوتی ہے۔\n ان مضامین کے کاتب کو بھی ظرافت سے کافی بہرہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ علاوہ دیگر مخترعات کے ”ہاسٹل میں پڑھنا“ کے عنوان کو ہر جگہ ”ہاسٹل پر پڑنا“بنا دیا ہے۔ مضمون میں ظرافت کی چاشنی پہلے ہی فقرے سے شروع ہے:\n ”ہم نے کالج میں تعلیم تو ضرور پائی اور رفتہ رفتہ بی اے بھی پاس کر لیا“۔ رفتہ رفتہ اور بھی کی معنویت دعوت نظر دیتی ہے آگے چل کر بی اے کے خانے اس خوبی سے گنوائے ہیں کہ بایدوشاید۔\n مضمون میں ایسے خاندان کی ذہنیت کا خاکہ ہے جو مہذب اور اخلاق پسندیدہ کا مالک ہونے کے باوصف قدامت پسند ہے اور حال کو ماضی کے آئینہ میں مشتبہ نظروں سے دیکھتا ہے۔ لڑکے نے انٹرنس کا امتحان تیسرے درجے میں پاس کیا ہے تاہم خوشیاں منائی جا رہی ہیں دعوتیں ہو رہی ہیں۔ مٹھائی تقسیم کی جا رہی ہے۔ خاندان خوش حال ہے مگر باوجود استطاعت کے لڑکے کو مزید تعلیم حاصل کرنے کے لئے ولایت نہ بھیجنے کی معقول ترین وجہ یہ ہے کہ گردو نواح سے کسی کا لڑکا ابھی تک ولایت نہ گیا تھا“۔\n بڑی ہمت کی تو لڑکے کو لاہور بھیج دیا مگرہاسٹل کے بجائے ایک ایسے اجنبی عزیز کے یہاں قیام کا فیصلہ کیا جاتا ہے جس سے رشتہ داری کی نوعیت معلوم کرنے کے لئےخاندانی شجرے کی ورق گردانی کرنا پڑتی ہے تاہم ہاسٹل پر اس کے گھر کو یہ کہہ کر ترجیح دی جاتی ہے کہ ”گھر پاکیزگی اور طہارت کا ایک کعبہ اور ہاسٹل گناہ ومعصیت کا دوزخ ہے“ ضمناً نفسیات کے اس پہلو پر روشنی پڑی کہ جذبات کو دبا کر تحت الشعور میں دھکیل دینا ان کو دُند مچانے کے لئے آزاد چھوڑ دینا اور ارتفاع میں مشکلیں حائل کرنایا ارتفاع سے محروم کر دینا ہے۔ پطرس کے الفاظ میں:\n ”اس سے تحصیل علم کا جو ایک ولولہ ہمارے دل میں اُٹھ رہا تھا وہ کچھ بیٹھ سا گیا۔ ہم نے سوچا ماموں لوگ (ماموں قسم کے لوگ؟) اپنی سرپرستی کے زعم میں والدین سے بھی زیادہ احتیاط برتیں گے۔ جس کا نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ ہمارے دماغی اور روحانی قوےٰ کو پھلنے پھولنے کا موقع نہ ملے گا اور تعلیم کا اصل مقصد فوت ہوجائے گا۔ چنانچہ وہی ہوا“۔\n بعد ازاں اس ”وہی ہوا“ کی شرح ہے۔ امتحانات میں پےدر پے فیل ہونا، صلاحیتوں کی بےراہ روی اختیار کرنا۔ صاف گوئی اور راستبازی کاکج مج راستے اختیار کرنا۔ غسل خانے میں چھپ چھپ کر سگریٹ پینا۔ المختصر وہ آزادی وفراخی ووارفتگی نصیب نہ ہوئی جو تعلیم کا اصل مقصد ہے“۔\n پطرس نے مسئلے کے اس پہلو کو ظریفانہ انداز میں اس حسن وخوبی سے وضاحت کی ہے کہ طبیعت عش عش کرتی ہے۔ تفصیل میں جانا مضمون کی لذتیت کو فنا کر دینا ہے۔ پڑھئے اور لطف اندوز ہوجائے۔\n کتاب کا مقصد بھی غالباً فوت ہو جائے گا اس کے مضامین کی چیر پھاڑ کی گئی۔ کتاب انگریزی کے اس مقولے کی بہترین ترجمان ہے کہ مذاق کے پردے میں بہت سی سنجیدہ باتیں The novel was first published in 7 parts in Khawateen Digest monthly from July 2007 to January 2008. It was later published as a complete novel by Ilm-o-Irfan Publishers. The story revolves around Ashar and Khirad\'s relationship with their daughter, Hareem, and how she unknowingly bridges the distances that exist between her parents. The novel is written in a retrospective manner and told mostly in flashbacks. The first half of the novel is based on mostly Ashar’s reflections and his point of view while the second part of the novel is told mainly from Khirad’s point of view.\n\nThe story has been adapted into a drama serial (Humsafar), produced by Momina Duraid and directed by Sarmad Sultan Khoosat.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4335300.Umera_Ahmed">About Umera Ahmed</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4335300.Umera_Ahmed"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1513085210p3/4335300.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16472117427964362481">Umera Ahmed is one of the most widely-read and popular Urdu fiction novelist and screenplay writer of this era. <br/>She completed her Masters in English Literature from Murray College, Sialkot. Later she became an English language lecturer for the students of O and A levels at Army Public College, Sialkot. However she left the job a few years back in order to devote her full attention to writing.<br/>She b</span>
  <span id="freeText16472117427964362481" style="display:none">Umera Ahmed is one of the most widely-read and popular Urdu fiction novelist and screenplay writer of this era. <br />She completed her Masters in English Literature from Murray College, Sialkot. Later she became an English language lecturer for the students of O and A levels at Army Public College, Sialkot. However she left the job a few years back in order to devote her full attention to writing.<br />She began her writing career in 1998 at a quite young age. Her initial stories were published in monthly urdu digests and later came out in the form of books. She has written about 16 books , comprising of complete novels and compilations of short stories. However it was her novel "Peer-e-Kaamil (S.A.W.W)" which became her identity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16472117427964362481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3295670">Quotes from پیر کامل</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;‗In life, at sometime or another we come to a point where all relationships cease—where there is only us and Allah. There are no parents, brother or sister, or any friend. Then we realise that there is no earth under us nor is there sky above, but only Allah who is supporting us in this emptiness. Then we realise our worth – it is not more than a grain of sand or the leaf of a plant. Then we realise our existence is only confined to our being. Our demise makes not a whit of difference to the world around us, nor to the scheme of things.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/670561-in-life-at-sometime-or-another-we-come-to-a">100 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;What is next to ecstasy?"<br />"Pain."<br />"What is next to pain?"<br />"Nothingness."<br />"What is next to nothingness?"<br />"Hell.&rdquo;</span>
